# 4.2.6 /api/v1/ai/cross_sell_matrix

## Quantifying ‚ÄúBought-Together‚Äù Affinity in One Call

## Purpose

Return a square matrix that quantifies how strongly each item or category lifts the probability of another being bought in the same basket.

---

### Business Use Cases

| **Business Play**                          | **Impact**               |
| ------------------------------------------ | ------------------------ |
| ‚ÄúFrequently Bought Together‚Äù widget        | +8‚Äì18% attach rate       |
| Dynamic bundle & upsell rules at checkout  | +5‚Äì12% AOV               |
| Assortment optimisation / planogram design | Higher shelf penetration |
| Category-to-category marketing flows       | 10‚Äì25% e-mail CTR        |

---

### Headers‚ÄÉ`X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yaml
POST  https://api-prod.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/cross_sell_matrix
Headers
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret:          <secret>
  Content-Type:      application/json
```

---

### Request Body ‚Äì Field-by-Field Guide

| **Key**        | **Type / Range**         | **Required**                    | **Meaning**                            | **Notes / Source**                |
| -------------- | ------------------------ | ------------------------------- | -------------------------------------- | --------------------------------- |
| `level`        | `"item"` or `"category"` | optional                        | Matrix granularity                     | Default: `"item"`                 |
| `customer_id`  | `string` or `null`       | optional                        | Set to get personal matrix             | Use global (null) or personal     |
| `transactions` | `array<object>`          | yes                             | Orders: each includes customer + items | 6‚Äì36 months history               |
| `item_catalog` | `array<object>`          | req. only if level = "category" | SKU to category mapping                | Needed if using `"category"` mode |

---

### transactions[]

| **Key**       | **Type**        | **Required** | **Description**            |
| ------------- | --------------- | ------------ | -------------------------- |
| `customer_id` | `string`        | yes          | Buyer ID                   |
| `items`       | `array<string>` | yes          | List of SKUs in the basket |

---

### item_catalog[] (for category mode)

| **Key**    | **Type** | **Required** | **Description** |
| ---------- | -------- | ------------ | --------------- |
| `item_id`  | `string` | yes          | SKU             |
| `category` | `string` | yes          | Category slug   |

---

### How the Metric Is Calculated

support(i) = number of orders with item i
support(i & j) = number of orders with both i and j
confidence(i ‚Üí j) = support(i & j) / support(i)

* Diagonal `(i == j)` = 1.0 by definition

* No negative values (min = 0)

* Optional: compute lift as `confidence / support(j)` downstream

---

### End-to-End Pipeline

1. Pre-clean: De-dupe `items[]` per order

2. Count: Map-reduce to count ``support(i)`` and `support(i & j)`

3. Compute: Calculate `confidence(i ‚Üí j)` and round

4. Reorder: Sort items by global frequency

5. Return: Include headers + matrix

---

### Example Request

```json
{
  "level": "item",
  "customer_id": null,
  "transactions": [
    { "customer_id": "C-1", "items": ["SKU-A1", "SKU-B9"] },
    { "customer_id": "C-2", "items": ["SKU-A1", "SKU-D7", "SKU-E2"] },
    { "customer_id": "C-1", "items": ["SKU-B9", "SKU-E2"] }
  ],
  "item_catalog": []
}
```

---

### Example Response

```json
{
  "items_or_categories": ["SKU-A1", "SKU-B9", "SKU-D7", "SKU-E2"],
  "matrix": [
    [1.0, 0.5, 0.5, 0.5],
    [0.5, 1.0, 0.0, 0.5],
    [1.0, 0.0, 1.0, 1.0],
    [0.5, 0.5, 0.5, 1.0]
  ],
  "metric": "orders_with_i_and_j / orders_with_i",
  "generated_at": "2025-05-21T10:33:37.149247Z"
}
```

---

### Field Glossary ‚Äì Response

| **Path**                | **Type**         | **Meaning**                         | **Use**                  |
| ----------------------- | ---------------- | ----------------------------------- | ------------------------ |
| `items_or_categories[]` | array of strings | Header mapping for matrix           | Display / lookup         |
| `matrix[][]`            | 2D float array   | Confidence(i‚Üíj) matrix              | Feed into UI or BI tools |
| `metric`                | string           | Formula used (default = confidence) | Analytics & audit        |
| `generated_at`          | ISO timestamp    | When this was calculated            | Cache strategy           |

---

### Threshold Recipes

| **Use Case**                     | **Rule**                                                                   | **Suggested Threshold**       |
| -------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------- |
| PDP ‚ÄúFrequently Bought Together‚Äù | Show top 3 `j` where `confidence(i‚Üíj) ‚â• 0.15`                              | 15% (fashion), 3‚Äì5% (grocery) |
| Cart Upsell                      | Auto-suggest `j` when `confidence(i‚Üíj) ‚â• 0.25` and high margin             | 25%                           |
| Bundle Creation                  | Export `i,j` pairs with `confidence ‚â• 0.30` and `support(i&j) ‚â• 100`       | 30%                           |
| E-mail Cross-sell                | Target buyers of `i` who‚Äôve never bought `j` with `confidence(i‚Üíj) ‚â• 0.20` | 20%                           |

---

### Engineering & Ops Tips

* Time window: 180d (CPG), 365d (furniture, B2B)

* Large baskets: Trim top 50 items by value if >200 SKUs

* Category mode: Requires `item_catalog`; ideal for long-tail items

* Global vs Personal: Global = all customers; Personal = 1:1

* Visualisation: Use seaborn heatmaps or D3.js chord diagrams

---

### Advanced Configuration (Enterprise)

| **Param**         | **Type**     | **Effect**                                      |
| ----------------- | ------------ | ----------------------------------------------- |
| `metric: "lift"`  | string       | Returns lift = confidence / support(j)          |
| `min_support`     | int ‚â• 1      | Filter items with low support count             |
| `symmetric: true` | boolean      | Averages matrix: `M[i][j] = M[j][i]`            |
| `time_range`      | {start, end} | Limit to transaction slice (e.g., Black Friday) |

---

### FAQ

| **Q**                       | **A**                                                         |
| --------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------- |
| How big can the matrix get? | Up to 5,000 √ó 5,000 (200 MB); sparse streaming coming Q4 2025 |
| Why are diagonals all 1.0?  | By definition: item always co-occurs with itself              |
| Any negative values?        | Never ‚Äì confidence is always ‚â• 0                              |
| Can I exclude items?        | Yes ‚Äì remove them from `transactions[].items` before calling  |
| Real-time latency?          | < 500ms for up to 250k orders                                 |

---

### Quick Win

Pipe the matrix into a rule that auto-inserts the top co-purchased SKU into your cart drawer.

Start with `confidence ‚â• 0.20` and watch AOV and attach rate climb.

---

# 4.2.7 /api/v1/ai/cross_sell_matrix

## Category-to-Category Heat-Map

## Purpose

The category-level mode aggregates every SKU into its parent category and tells you:

‚ÄúWhen a basket contains any item from category i, how often does it also contain at least one item from category j?‚Äù

Use-cases range from macro merchandising to campaign adjacency rules.

---

### Commercial Playbook

| **Commercial Play**            | **How the Matrix Helps**                                            | **Typical Lift**     |
| ------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------- |
| Homepage ‚ÄúComplete the Look‚Äù   | Display the top companion categories while browsing a base category | +6‚Äì10% click-through |
| Joint discount bundles         | Identify pairings with high co-occurrence but low margin to bundle  | +4‚Äì8% basket value   |
| Store layout / aisle adjacency | Co-locate categories with high mutual confidence                    | +3‚Äì5% in-store sales |
| Cross-category e-mail flows    | Target buyers who skipped a usually-linked category                 | 2‚Äì3√ó better response |

---

### Headers‚ÄÉ`X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yaml
POST  https://api-prod.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/cross_sell_matrix
Headers
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret:          <secret>
  Content-Type:      application/json
```

---

### Request Body (Category Mode)

```json
{
  "level": "category",
  "transactions": [
    { "customer_id": "C-1", "items": ["SKU-A1", "SKU-B9"] },
    { "customer_id": "C-2", "items": ["SKU-A1", "SKU-D7", "SKU-E2"] },
    { "customer_id": "C-3", "items": ["SKU-D7"] },
    { "customer_id": "C-4", "items": ["SKU-A1", "SKU-E2"] },
    { "customer_id": "C-1", "items": ["SKU-B9", "SKU-E2"] },
    { "customer_id": "C-5", "items": ["SKU-A1", "SKU-B9", "SKU-D7"] },
    { "customer_id": "C-6", "items": ["SKU-E2", "SKU-D7"] }
  ],
  "item_catalog": [
    { "item_id": "SKU-A1", "category": "Shoes" },
    { "item_id": "SKU-B9", "category": "Shoes" },
    { "item_id": "SKU-D7", "category": "Accessories" },
    { "item_id": "SKU-E2", "category": "Wearables" }
  ]
}
```

---

### Field-by-Field

| **Path**         | **Type**         | **Required?** | **Meaning**                      | **Tips**                          |
| ---------------- | ---------------- | ------------- | -------------------------------- | --------------------------------- |
| `level`          | `"category"`     | ‚úÖ             | Triggers category aggregation    | `"item"` is default               |
| `transactions[]` | `array<object>`  | ‚úÖ             | 1 transaction = 1 order          | Clean out test or canceled orders |
| `item_catalog[]` | `array<object>`  | ‚úÖ             | SKU ‚Üí Category map               | Many-to-one is valid              |
| `customer_id`    | `string or null` | optional      | Set for personal matrix (1-to-1) | Keep `null` for global stats      |

---

### Computation Logic

1. SKU ‚Üí Category: Every SKU becomes its category. Categories are de-duplicated per basket.

2. Support counts:

* support(i) = baskets with category i

* support(i & j) = baskets with both i and j

3. Confidence:

confidence(i ‚Üí j) = orders_with_both(i, j) / orders_with_i

* Diagonal = 1.0

4. Ordering: Categories sorted by descending global support for consistency.

---

### Response

{
  "items_or_categories": ["Accessories", "Shoes", "Wearables"],
  "matrix": [
    [1.0, 0.5, 0.5],
    [0.4, 1.0, 0.6],
    [0.5, 0.75, 1.0]
  ],
  "metric": "orders_with_i_and_j / orders_with_i",
  "generated_at": "2025-05-21T10:42:59.767166Z"
}

---

### Interpretation Highlights

* Wearables ‚Üí Shoes = 0.75
‚Üí 75% of baskets with Wearables also have Shoes ‚Äî strong attach rate.

* Shoes ‚Üí Accessories = 0.40
‚Üí Moderate co-occurrence; could justify cross-sell or small bundle.

---

### Practical Thresholds & Actions

| **Confidence(i‚Üíj)** | **Interpretation** | **Suggested Action**                        |
| ------------------- | ------------------ | ------------------------------------------- |
| ‚â• 0.70              | Must-have pair     | Auto-bundle, display ‚ÄúComplete the Look‚Äù UI |
| 0.30 ‚Äì 0.69         | Strong link        | Use for e-mail flows, cross-sell thumbnails |
| 0.10 ‚Äì 0.29         | Weak link          | Only use if margin is high                  |
| < 0.10              | Likely noise       | Ignore to reduce UI clutter                 |

---

### SQL Recipe ‚Äì Category Pair Counts

```SQL
WITH sku_orders AS (
  SELECT o.order_id, p.category
  FROM orders o
  JOIN order_items oi ON oi.order_id = o.order_id
  JOIN products p ON p.sku = oi.sku
  WHERE o.order_date >= DATE_SUB(CURRENT_DATE(), INTERVAL 12 MONTH)
),
pairs AS (
  SELECT o1.category AS cat_i, o2.category AS cat_j, o1.order_id
  FROM sku_orders o1
  JOIN sku_orders o2 ON o1.order_id = o2.order_id
)
SELECT
  cat_i,
  cat_j,
  COUNT(DISTINCT order_id) AS orders_with_i_and_j
FROM pairs
GROUP BY 1, 2;
```

---

### Commercial Recipes (Category-Level)

| **Scenario**             | **Usage**                                              | **Expected KPI**         |
| ------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------ | ------------------------ |
| Paid search landing page | Add tabs for top co-bought categories                  | +8% session depth        |
| Category hero banners    | Show multi-category bundles (e.g., Shoes + Smartwatch) | +5% CTR                  |
| Stock & demand planning  | Allocate buffer stock to co-bought categories          | Fewer stockouts in promo |
| Loyalty incentives       | Give bonus points for Accessories if Shoes in cart     | +12% attach rate         |

---

### Advanced Parameters (Enterprise)

| **Param**         | **Allowed Values** | **Purpose**                                     |
| ----------------- | ------------------ | ----------------------------------------------- |
| `metric`          | `"lift"`           | Shows lift vs baseline purchase rate            |
| `min_support`     | `int ‚â• 5`          | Drop rare categories to reduce noise            |
| `time_range`      | `{start, end}`     | Slice matrix by time (e.g., Black Friday week)  |
| `symmetric: true` | `true/false`       | Average matrix for symmetric display (graphing) |

---

### FAQ

| **Q**                                                 | **A**                                                     |
| ----------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------------------------------------- |
| I have 5,000 SKUs and 30 categories ‚Äì is this faster? | Yes ‚Äì runtime scales with categories¬≤, not SKUs           |
| Repeated categories in a basket ‚Äî do they inflate?    | No ‚Äì duplicates removed before counting                   |
| Can I rename categories?                              | Yes ‚Äì rename in `item_catalog` before sending             |
| Sparse personal matrix ‚Äî all 0/1s ‚Äî why?              | Too little data; use 6‚Äì12 mo window or fallback to global |
| Recompute how often?                                  | Weekly (global), daily (real-time cart flows)             |
| Privacy concerns?                                     | Only customer\_id is used (can be hashed); no PII needed  |

---

### Next Step

Feed the category-level matrix into your recommendation engine.
When a shopper adds a category like Shoes, query the matrix and surface top SKUs from the highest-confidence follower category (e.g., Accessories).

* Result: Higher attach rate and AOV ‚Äî no discounts required.

---

# 4.2.8 /api/v1/ai/dynamic_pricing_recommend

## AI-Driven Price Optimisation in <150 ms\

## Purpose

One call returns the profit- or revenue-maximising price for a SKU, using a micro-trained demand model that considers:

* Historical sell-through

* Competitor prices

* Current inventory

* Shopper context (channel/country)

## Typical lift:

+3‚Äì9% gross margin or +4‚Äì12% top-line revenue (validated in 14 retailers).

---

### Headers `X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yaml
POST  https://api-prod.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/dynamic_pricing_recommend
Headers
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret:          <secret>
  Content-Type:      application/json
```

---

### Business Value

| **Scenario**              | **How this endpoint helps**                           | **Impact**                 |
| ------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------- |
| Daily price suggestion    | Scheduled call uploads updated prices to POS / web    | +4‚Äì6% gross profit         |
| Flash sale tuning         | Frequent calls optimize discount velocity and margins | Sell aged stock 30% faster |
| Competitor price matching | Undercuts rivals only if margin stays healthy         | Hold share, protect margin |
| Marketplace auto-repricer | Trigger on every new bid                              | +15‚Äì25% Buy Box win rate   |

---

### Request Body ‚Äì Schema & Field Descriptions

| **Field**                  | **Type / Range**           | **Required** | **Description**                              |
| -------------------------- | -------------------------- | ------------ | -------------------------------------------- |
| `product_id`               | `string`                   | ‚úÖ           | SKU to price                                |
| `cost_per_unit`            | `float ‚â• 0`                | ‚úÖ           | Landed cost incl. logistics                 |
| `optimize_for`             | \`"profit"                 | "revenue"    | ‚úÖ                                          |
| `candidate_prices`         | `array<float>`             | ‚úÖ           | Price points to evaluate                    |
| `historical[]`             | `array<object> (‚â•10 rows)` | ‚úÖ           | Recent sales data to train the model        |
| `competitor_price_current` | `float`                    | optional     | Live rival price (defaults to last observed) |
| `inventory_level_current`  | `int`                      | optional     | Current stock level                          |
| `segment_current`          | `object`                   | optional     | Contextual info: channel, country, etc.      |

---

### Historical Row Fields

| **Field**          | **Type**   | **Required** | **Description**                               |
| ------------------ | ---------- | ------------ | --------------------------------------------- |
| `date`             | `ISO date` | ‚úÖ            | Day of sale                                  |
| `price`            | `float`    | ‚úÖ            | Price used that day                          |
| `units_sold`       | `int ‚â• 0`  | ‚úÖ            | Quantity sold                                |
| `competitor_price` | `float`    | optional     | Rival price on same day                       |
| `inventory_level`  | `int ‚â• 0`  | optional     | Inventory at start of day                     |
| `segment`          | `object`   | optional     | e.g., `{ "channel": "web", "country": "BR" }` |

---

### Sample Request

```json
{
  "product_id": "SKU-123",
  "cost_per_unit": 50.0,
  "optimize_for": "profit",
  "candidate_prices": [79.0, 89.0, 99.0, 109.0],
  "historical": [
    { "date": "2025-03-01", "price": 99.0, "units_sold": 38, "competitor_price": 95.0, "inventory_level": 180, "segment": { "channel": "web", "country": "BR" } },
    { "date": "2025-03-02", "price": 99.0, "units_sold": 41, "competitor_price": 96.0, "inventory_level": 170, "segment": { "channel": "web", "country": "BR" } },
    ...
    { "date": "2025-03-10", "price": 109.0, "units_sold": 25, "competitor_price": 103.0, "inventory_level": 200, "segment": { "channel": "store", "country": "BR" } }
  ],
  "competitor_price_current": 94.0,
  "inventory_level_current": 120,
  "segment_current": { "channel": "mobile", "country": "BR" }
}
```

---

### Engine Workflow (Simplified)

1. Clean & encode data (e.g., one-hot segment, log transform).

2. Train ElasticNet, XGBoost, Random Forest on 75% of history.

3. Extract demand elasticity.

4. Predict demand per price in candidate_prices.

5. Compute:

* revenue = price √ó expected_units

* profit = (price ‚Äì cost) √ó expected_units

6. Select best_price based on objective (profit or revenue).

7. Apply guardrails (min margin, max discount).

8. Return prediction.

9. Log for drift monitoring.

---

### Response

```json
{
  "best_price": 79.0,
  "outcomes": [
    { "candidate_price": 79.0, "expected_units": 85.0, "expected_revenue": 6714.9, "expected_profit": 2464.96 },
    { "candidate_price": 89.0, "expected_units": 61.13, "expected_revenue": 5440.35, "expected_profit": 2383.97 },
    { "candidate_price": 99.0, "expected_units": 44.56, "expected_revenue": 4411.79, "expected_profit": 2183.61 },
    { "candidate_price": 109.0, "expected_units": 35.23, "expected_revenue": 3839.86, "expected_profit": 2078.46 }
  ],
  "model_info": {
    "algorithm": "XGBoost",
    "mape": 0.0,
    "train_rows": 10
  },
  "interpretation": "Setting the price at 79.00 maximises PROFIT: +3.4% versus the next-best option (89.00) given today‚Äôs competitor price (94.0) and inventory level (120 units)."
}
```

---

### Response Fields

| **Field**              | **Type** | **Description**                  | **Use Case**               |
| ---------------------- | -------- | -------------------------------- | -------------------------- |
| `best_price`           | `float`  | Optimal price                    | Push to web/POS            |
| `outcomes[]`           | `array`  | Simulated results per candidate  | Build price ladders        |
| ‚Ü≥ `expected_units`     | `float`  | Forecasted demand                | Plan inventory or ops      |
| ‚Ü≥ `expected_revenue`   | `float`  | Price √ó Units                    | ‚Äî                          |
| ‚Ü≥ `expected_profit`    | `float`  | (Price ‚Äì Cost) √ó Units           | ‚Äî                          |
| `model_info.algorithm` | `string` | Chosen ML model                  | ML audit                   |
| `model_info.mape`      | `float`  | Mean Absolute % Error (hold-out) | Trigger retrain if > 0.2   |
| `interpretation`       | `string` | Plain-English summary            | Show in pricing dashboards |

---

### Commercial Playbooks

| **Use-case**         | **Recipe**                                                             | **KPI Lift**             |
| -------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------ |
| Clear slow movers    | Use `[cost√ó1.05, cost√ó1.1‚Ä¶]`, optimize\_for: `"revenue"`               | Free DC space 25% faster |
| Flagship products    | Call every 2h if `MAPE < 0.10`; widen price range if `elasticity > -2` | Protect margin & share   |
| End-of-season sale   | Set `cost=0`; maximize revenue                                         | +8‚Äì12% clearance revenue |
| Channel segmentation | Call twice: `segment_current.channel = web` vs. `store`                | AOV +3%, Profit +4%      |

---

### Engineering & Ops Tips

* Candidate grid: Try 4‚Äì8 prices near current tag

* Psychology-aware: Include .90, .99 variants

* Lagging competitor: Use competitor_price_current explicitly

* Inventory spike: Narrow grid to preserve margin

* Batch nightly: Loop SKUs, push best prices to ERP

* A/B test: +10% pricing to 10% traffic to measure elasticity

---

### FAQ

| **Q**                                    | **A**                                                        |
| ---------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------ |
| What if `MAPE = 0.00`?                   | Likely only 1 hold-out row; add more historical data.        |
| Minimum distinct prices?                 | At least two ‚Äì otherwise no curve fitting possible.          |
| Can I add features like weekday/weather? | Yes ‚Äì include as columns in `historical[]`; auto-encoded.    |
| Currency format?                         | Use same currency throughout; endpoint is currency-agnostic. |
| How to set pricing guardrails?           | Use header: `X-Min-Margin-Pct: 0.25` (Enterprise only).      |

---

### Next Step

Feed yesterday‚Äôs sales snapshot into this endpoint with 4‚Äì8 candidate prices.
Then push the `best_price` to your e-commerce, store POS or marketplace.
Measure margin lift in days ‚Äì most clients break even on implementation in < 30 days.

---

# 4.2.9 /api/v1/ai/uplift_model

## Individual-level causal lift scoring

## Purpose

Identify who‚Äôs truly persuadable (and who isn‚Äôt) before you send your next campaign.
The endpoint ingests treatment / control outcomes and returns an incremental-lift (uplift) score for every single customer plus decile roll-ups.
Typical usage: mail only the top‚Äê2 uplift deciles and hold out the bottom two, slashing CAC 25-40 % while keeping the same conversions.

---

### Headers `X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yml
POST  https://api-prod.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/uplift_model
Headers
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret:          <secret>
  Content-Type:      application/json
```

  ---

### Business Value

| **Pain-point**                        | **How the endpoint helps**                                                                | **Typical lift**                               |
| ------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------- |
| Spray-and-pray campaigns waste budget | Scores ‚Äútrue-positives‚Äù (= will buy because of the promo) vs. sure-things & never-buyers. | ‚Äì30 % send volume at flat conversions          |
| Costly hold-outs                      | Automatically produces control deciles (negative uplift) for statistically sound tests.   | +5-8 pp improvement in net incremental revenue |
| Complex in-house causal ML            | Micro-trains a model in < 30 s; no infra to maintain.                                     | Deploy in 1 sprint                             |

---

### Request Body ‚Äì Every Field

| **JSON path** | **Type / Range** | **Req.?** | **Meaning**                                                            | **Notes**                  |
| ------------- | ---------------- | --------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------- |
| contamination | 0 ‚Ä¶ 1            | optional  | Share of control users who were accidentally exposed to treatment.     | Default 0.0                |
| rows[]       | array<object>    | yes       | Min 200 rows. Each row needs ‚Ä¶                                         |                            |
| ‚Ü≥ id          | string           | yes       | Customer identifier.                                                   | Returned verbatim.         |
| ‚Ü≥ treatment   | 0 \| 1           | yes       | 1 = received campaign/exposure                                         | Binary only.               |
| ‚Ü≥ outcome     | 0 \| 1           | yes       | 1 = converted / purchased                                              | Define your success event. |
| ‚Ü≥ features.* | number \| string | yes       | Any mix of numeric & categorical predictors (age, country, RFM, etc.). | Auto one-hot / scaling.    |

* Data sufficiency rule ‚Äì at least 200 rows and > 0 variants of both treatment & outcome ‚Üí else request is rejected.

```SQL
{
  // ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  //  üéØ  INDIVIDUAL-LEVEL UPLIFT SCORING  ‚Äì  POST  /api/uplift_model
  //  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
  //  What this route does
  //  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  //  ‚Ä¢ Accepts **treatment / control** data and estimates the incremental
  //    impact (‚Äúuplift‚Äù, i.e. *causal lift*) of a campaign **for every customer**.
  //  ‚Ä¢ Internals:
  //        ‚Äì If the library **causalml** is available the endpoint runs an
  //          `UpliftRandomForestClassifier` (KL criterion).
  //        ‚Äì Otherwise it falls back to a **T-Learner**: two separate
  //          Gradient-Boosting Models (one on treated rows, one on control).
  //  ‚Ä¢ Requires **‚â• 200 rows** for a stable model (binary *treatment* & *outcome*).
  //
  //  Field-by-field specification
  //  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  //  ‚Ä¢ rows[] (array)          :  Each object **must** contain:
  //        ‚Äì id          (string) : Unique customer ID.
  //        ‚Äì treatment    (0|1)   : 1 = received campaign / was exposed.
  //        ‚Äì outcome      (0|1)   : 1 = converted / purchased / subscribed.
  //        ‚Äì features     (object): Arbitrary numeric or categorical fields
  //                                  (age, country, prior_purchases, ‚Ä¶).
  //                                  Categorical keys are one-hot-encoded auto-
  //                                  matically ‚Äì you can mix types freely.
  //
  //  What the response means
  //  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  //  ‚Ä¢ `average_treatment_effect` ‚Äì global ATE across all rows (positive = good).
  //  ‚Ä¢ `decile_summary[]`         ‚Äì mean uplift & #customers in each decile
  //                                 (1 = lowest, 10 = highest uplift).
  //  ‚Ä¢ `details[]`                ‚Äì per-customer uplift score and assigned decile
  //                                 so you can pick top-decile customers for the
  //                                 next wave and hold out the bottom decile.
  //
  //  Practical reading
  //  ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  //  ‚Ä¢ High positive **uplift_score** ‚Üí customer is MORE likely to convert if
  //    targeted ‚Äì prioritise for campaigns.
  //  ‚Ä¢ Negative score ‚Üí persuasion-proof segment (or even net-negative) ‚Äì skip
  //    or A/B-test cautiously.
  //
  //  ---------------------------------------------------------------------------
  //  ‚Üì  Stub payload ‚Äì paste ‚â• 200 real rows in ‚Äúrows[]‚Äù before sending
  // ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ‚îÄ
  "contamination": 0.15,
  "rows": [
    { "id": "C-001", "treatment": 1, "outcome": 1, "features": { "age": 34, "country": "BR", "prior_purchases": 2 } },
    { "id": "C-002", "treatment": 0, "outcome": 0, "features": { "age": 27, "country": "US", "prior_purchases": 0 } },

```

---

### What Happens Under the Hood

1. Pre-process ‚Äì handle contamination (re-weights control), one-hot categories, scale numerics.

2. Model selection

* If causalml lib present ‚ñ∂Ô∏é UpliftRandomForestClassifier (KL criterion).

* Else T-Learner (two Gradient-Boosting trees).

3. Cross-validation √ó 3 folds ‚Üí choose hyper-parameters with highest Qini uplift.

4. Score each row: P(outcome | treat) ‚Äì P(outcome | control) ‚Üí uplift_score.

5. Rank & bucket into ten equal-sized deciles.

6. Return global ATE, conversion rates, decile table & per-ID details. Average latency: < 40 s on 50 k rows (CPU).

---

        }
    ],
    "interpretation": "Treatment group converted at 63.81% vs control 25.71% (ATE +0.386).  **Decile 10** contains 21 customers with mean uplift +1.000, representing ‚âà 21.0 additional conversions if fully targeted.  **Decile 1**‚Äôs mean uplift is -0.999 ‚Äî ideal as a hold-out or cost-control segment."
}
```

---

### Path

| Path                       | Meaning                      | How to act                                   |
| -------------------------- | ---------------------------- | -------------------------------------------- |
| average_treatment_effect   | Global incremental lift.     | > 0 ‚Üí campaign works; < 0 ‚Üí re-think.        |
| decile_summary[]           | Mean uplift by 10 % buckets. | Target deciles 8-10, test 5-7, suppress 1-2. |
| details[]                  | Per-customer score & bucket. | Feed top deciles into ESP / CRM segment.     |

---

### Activation Recipes

| Goal                   | Playbook                                                      | KPI impact                    |
| ---------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------- | ----------------------------- |
| Email blast cost-cut   | Send only deciles 8-10; keep 3-4 for future; never email 1-2. | ‚Äì35 % send cost, flat orders  |
| Personalised discounts | Give 10 % off to decile 10, 5 % to 8-9, none to others.       | Same revenue, half promo cost |
| A/B hold-out           | Use decile 1 as natural control in follow-up experiment.      | Robust incrementality proof   |

---

### Engineering Tips

* Cold-start customers ‚Äì set treatment=0, outcome=0, include features; they‚Äôll still be scored via model priors.

* Categorical explosions ‚Äì cap rare categories (< 100 rows) into ‚ÄúOther‚Äù to keep trees shallow.

* Feature drift ‚Äì if ‚â• 2 categorical values disappear for > 30 days, re-train.

* Minimum decile size ‚Äì endpoint enforces ‚â• 15 rows; else merges neighbouring buckets.

* Storing scores ‚Äì upsert uplift_decile column in your CDP for fast audience builds.

---

### Next step
Run a one-off call on last campaign‚Äôs data, export the top two uplift deciles, and launch a 72-h retargeting email. Measure incremental revenue v. hold-out ‚Äì most clients break even in the first blast.

---

# 4.3 Forecasting & Planning

## Forecasting & Planning

`forecast_revenue`, `forecast_units`, `forecast_units_asyncio`, `forecast_cost`, `forecast_cost_improved`

---

# 4.3.1 /api/v1/ai/forecast_revenue

## Purpose
Generate a 12-month revenue outlook (calendar & business days), pick the best model automatically, and get back ready-to-plot numbers plus error diagnostics.

---

### Headers `X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yml
POST https://api.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/forecast_revenue
headers:
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret: <secret>
  Content-Type: application/json
```

---

### Why you‚Äôll use it

| Business question                           | How the route helps                                                                                      | Typical win                        |
| ------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------- |
| ‚ÄúHow much cash do we book next quarter?‚Äù    | Outputs monthly forecast with 80 % & 95 % CIs (not shown in sample).                                     | Replaces xls extrapolations in 5 s |
| ‚ÄúWhich model should we trust?‚Äù              | Benchmarks ARIMA, Prophet, ETS, TBATS, Aggregation (na√Øve), etc., selects the lowest RMSE automatically. | No data-science headcount needed   |
| ‚ÄúOps wants both calendar & business views.‚Äù | Returns two matrices: one counting all days, one excluding weekends/holidays.                            | Direct feed into FP\&A dashboards  |

---

### Request body ‚Äì every field

| Path             | Type       | Req.? | Meaning                  | Notes                                    |
| ---------------- | ---------- | ----- | ------------------------ | ---------------------------------------- |
| forecast_period  | int ‚â• 1    | yes   | # months to predict      | Typical 6-, 12-, 18-month horizons       |
| data[]           | array      | yes   | Historical daily revenue | Needs ‚â• 60 rows (‚âà 2 months)             |
| ‚Ü≥ date           | YYYY-MM-DD | yes   | Day in ISO format        | Gaps allowed; endpoint auto-fills zeroes |
| ‚Ü≥ revenue        | float ‚â• 0  | yes   | Gross revenue that day   | Same currency every row                  |

---

### What happens under the hood

1. Pre-process ‚Äì sort, fill missing days ‚Üí 0 revenue, detect outliers (IQR winsorise), box-cox if needed.

2. Model zoo ‚Äì ARIMA, STL-ETS, Prophet, TBATS, Croston (if > 40 % zeros) + Aggregation benchmark.

3. Cross-validation ‚Äì rolling origin (4 folds) scoring RMSE & MAPE.

4. Champion select ‚Äì lowest weighted RMSE (calendar 0.6 √ó business 0.4).

5. Post-process ‚Äì make sure predictions ‚â• 0; re-add outliers if suppressed.

6. Return forecast + error table + run-time.

Average latency: ~0.3 s on 90 days history; scales linearly.

---

---

### Field

| Field                | How to read                                | Action                                                             |
| -------------------- | ------------------------------------------ | -----------------------------------------------------------------  |
| best_algorithm       | Model with lowest cross-val error.         | Track changes ‚Äì if it flips often you may have structural breaks.  |
| evaluation_metrics   | RMSE / MAE (absolute), R¬≤ (explained var.) | MAE ‚â§ 10 % of mean ‚áí ‚Äúgood‚Äù; else inspect seasonality or promos   |
| forecast.calendar[]  | Revenue including weekends & holidays.     | Feed to top-line board decks.                                      |
| forecast.business[]  | Revenue excluding weekends/holidays.       | Feed to capacity & staffing planning.                              |

---

### Power-user tips

* Promo bumps ‚Äì send an extra boolean column `promo_day`: the API auto-segments regime switches (beta preview).

* Currency roll-ups ‚Äì if you mix multi-currency streams, convert externally first; endpoint expects single unit.

* Edge series (< 60 pts) ‚Äì fallback to ‚ÄúAggregation‚Äù by design ‚Üí consider weekly aggregation then re-call.

* Scenario testing ‚Äì call twice: once full history, once minus last promo month ‚Üí quantify uplift delta.

---

### Next step
Run the endpoint weekly, store `forecast.calendar` in your BI layer, and chart actual vs forecast. Alert finance if ¬±10 % deviation materialises for two consecutive weeks ‚Äî teams can re-allocate paid-media budget in-flight.

---

# 4.3.2 /api/v1/ai/forecast_units

## One-Shot SKU-Level Demand Forecast

## Purpose

Call once, get a 6-month, day-to-business-day unit forecast for an individual SKU ‚Äì automatically benchmarks statistical & ML models and returns the winner with diagnostics.

---

### Headers `X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yml
POST https://api.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/forecast_units
headers:
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret: <secret>
  Content-Type: application/json
```

---

### When you‚Äôll reach for it

| Business question                                         | How the route answers                                                                                  | Typical payoff                                 |
| --------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------- |
| ‚ÄúHow many pieces should we replenish per SKU each month?‚Äù | Calendar & business-day unit forecast plus ¬±2 œÉ error band (not shown below).               | Cuts stock-out/over-stock cost without spreadsheet kung-fu|
| ‚ÄúWhich model works for lumpy demand?‚Äù                     | Runs ARIMA, TBATS, Prophet, Random-Forest, Gradient Boost, Croston (intermittent) & picks lowest RMSE. | Gives Croston/ML without writing a line of code|
| ‚ÄúOps wants the figure in pieces, not revenue.‚Äù            | Accepts sales_quantity straight from POS/OMS.                                                          | No price inflation noise                       |

---

### Request body ‚Äì every key explained

| Path              | Type       | Req.? | Meaning                | Notes                       |
| ----------------- | ---------- | ----- | ---------------------- | --------------------------  |
| product_code      | string     | yes   | SKU or internal code   | Returned as-is in response  |
| forecast_period   | int ‚â• 1    | yes   | Months to predict      | 3, 6, 12 typical            |
| data[]            | array      | yes   | Daily historical units | ‚â• 45 rows recommended       |
| ‚Ü≥ date            | YYYY-MM-DD | yes   | ISO calendar date      | Gaps auto-filled with 0     |
| ‚Ü≥ sales_quantity  | int ‚â• 0    | yes   | Units sold that day    | Same UoM entire series      |

```json

    { "date": "2025-04-11", "sales_quantity": 16 },

    { "date": "2025-04-14", "sales_quantity": 18 },

    { "date": "2025-04-16", "sales_quantity": 16 },
    { "date": "2025-04-17", "sales_quantity": 17 },
    { "date": "2025-04-18", "sales_quantity": 16 },
    { "date": "2025-04-19", "sales_quantity": 9  },
    { "date": "2025-04-20", "sales_quantity": 8  }
  ]
}
```

---

### Behind the curtain

1. Cleaning ‚Äì sort, fill missing dates (=0), Hampel filter outliers (kept but flagged).

2. Feature crafting ‚Äì lag-7/14/28, promo/holiday flags (if extra cols present), rolling means.

3. Model zoo ‚Äì Seasonal-ARIMA, STL-ETS, Prophet, TBATS, Random-Forest Regressor, Gradient-Boost, Croston for intermittent.

4. Cross-val ‚Äì expanding window, score RMSE/MAE/R¬≤.

5. Champion ‚Äì lowest RMSE (ties ‚Üí lowest MAE).

6. Forecast ‚Äì horizon = forecast_period * 30/30.4 calendar & biz-day splits.

7. Safety floor ‚Äì clip negatives ‚Üí 0.

8. Return JSON + run-time (seconds).

---

---

### Field

| Field                 | How to read                    | Action                                                                             |
| --------------------- | ------------------------------ | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| best_algorithm        | Model with lowest RMSE.        | Track per-SKU ‚Äì if it flips to Croston your item may have become slow-moving.      |
| average_daily_sales   | Mean of historical series.     | Quick reasonableness check: forecast shouldn‚Äôt diverge > ¬±30 % unless seasonality. |
| forecast.calendar[]   | Units incl. weekends/holidays. | Feed to S\&OP, supplier POs.                                                       |
| forecast.business[]   | Units excl. weekends.          | Feed to labour & picking slot planning.                                            |

---

### Common gotchas & pro tips

* Intermittent demand ‚Äì ‚â• 40 % zero days? The route auto-tests Croston & TSB ‚Äì flag appears in `evaluation_metrics.model_candidates` (omit here for brevity).

* Promotions ‚Äì add a boolean `promo` column; tree models ingest it, improving spikes.

* Multi-channel split ‚Äì want web vs store? Call the endpoint separately per channel code.

* Very new SKUs ‚Äì < 30 data points defaults to ‚ÄúNa√Øve mean‚Äù and adds `"note":"cold-start"` in metrics.

---

### Next step

Schedule the call on the 1st business day each month, write `forecast.business` into your ERP replenishment table, and compare actual vs forecast weekly; auto-trigger a re-forecast if absolute error > 20 % for two consecutive weeks.

---

# 4.3.3 /api/v1/ai/forecast_cost

### One-shot daily cost projection

**Purpose**‚ÄÉForecast the total daily COGS/OPEX (or any cost series) out six months.  
The service auto-benchmarks classic time-series models against tree-based ML, picks the champion, and returns both calendar-day and business-day aggregates.

---

### Headers‚ÄÉ`X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yml
POST `https://api.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/forecast_cost`
headers:
X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
X-Secret: <secret>
Content-Type: application/json
```

---


---

### Why you‚Äôd call it

| Business question                          | How the route helps                                                                        | Typical payoff                                      |
|------------------------------------------  |------------------------------------------------------------------------                    |-----------------------------------------------------|
| ‚ÄúHow much cash will we burn next quarter?‚Äù | 6-month cost forecast with statistical diagnostics.                                        | Informs cash-flow planning, treasury hedging.       |
| ‚ÄúWhich model should finance trust?‚Äù        | Cross-validates ARIMA / ETS / Prophet / TBATS / tree ML and returns the lowest-error pick. | Eliminates manual model selection.                  |
| ‚ÄúNeed weekends vs workdays split.‚Äù         | Returns calendar and business series side-by-side.                                         | Feeds both GL accruals and FP&A staffing models.    |

---

### Request body ‚Äì field dictionary

| Path            | Type        | Req? | Meaning                          | Notes                                               |
|---------------  |-------------|----- |--------------------------------- |-----------------------------------------------------|
| forecast_period | int ‚â• 1     | ‚úîÔ∏é    | Number of months to predict      | 3, 6, 12 common                                     |
| data[]          | array       | ‚úîÔ∏é    | Historic daily cost              | ‚â• 45 rows recommended                               |
| ‚Ü≥ date          | YYYY-MM-DD  | ‚úîÔ∏é    | ISO date                         | Gaps auto-filled with 0                             |
| ‚Ü≥ cost          | number      | ‚úîÔ∏é    | Cost on that date (same currency)| Negative values allowed (rebates)                   |


---

```json
{
  "forecast_period": 6,
  "data": [
    { "date": "2025-01-01", "cost": 1100.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-02", "cost": 1112.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-03", "cost": 1118.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-04", "cost": 1083.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-05", "cost": 1078.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-06", "cost": 1125.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-07", "cost": 1130.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-08", "cost": 1136.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-09", "cost": 1142.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-10", "cost": 1148.00 },
    { "date": "2025-01-11", "cost": 1105.00 },

---

## How it works under the hood

- **Pre-processing** ‚Äî sort, fill missing dates, Hampel filter outliers (flagged).  
- **Feature engineering** ‚Äî lag 7/14/28, month & weekday dummies, moving averages.  
- **Model zoo** ‚Äî Seasonal-ARIMA, ETS, STL-TBATS, Prophet, Random-Forest, Gradient-Boost.  
- **Validation** ‚Äî expanding-window CV ‚Üí RMSE/MAE/R¬≤.  
- **Champion selection** ‚Äî lowest RMSE (tie-break: lower MAE).  
- **Forecast horizon** ‚Äî forecast_period √ó 30 calendar days, then roll-up to month-level calendar & biz-day.  
- **Post-process** ‚Äî negatives are clipped to 0; adds two-sigma error band (not shown here).  
- **Return** ‚Äî JSON + run-time.

---

## Reference response explained

```json
{
  "forecast_period": 6,
  "forecast_result": {
    "analysis_type": "generic_cost",
    "best_algorithm": "Aggregation",
    "evaluation_metrics": {
      "RMSE": 31.871275523384387,
      "MAE": 26.72328927342509,
      "R2": 0.225582055790993,
      "average_daily_cost": 1466.3052433749297,
      "Interpretation": "The Aggregation algorithm was selected because it achieved a low RMSE of 31.87, MAE of 26.72, and R¬≤ of 0.23. The average daily cost forecast is 1466.31."
    },
    "forecast": {
      "calendar": [
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-04", "value": 45003.125869601354 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-05", "value": 46503.23006525473 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-06", "value": 45003.125869601354 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-07", "value": 46503.23006525473 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-08", "value": 46503.23006525473 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-09", "value": 45003.125869601354 }
      ],
      "business": [
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-04", "value": 33002.29230437432 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-05", "value": 33002.29230437432 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-06", "value": 31502.188108720948 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-07", "value": 34502.3965000277 },
        { "yyyy-mm": "2025-08", "value": 31502.188108720948 },

```

---

## Field

| Field                | How to read                                     | Suggested action                                                     |
| -------------------- | ----------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| best_algorithm       | Winner of the bake-off.                         | Track per series; sudden switch to ML may indicate structural break. |
| average_daily_cost   | Mean of the historic series.                    | Quick sense-check vs budget.                                         |
| calendar             | 100 % of days, weekends included.               | Use for cash-flow burn rate.                                         |
| business             | Mon-Fri (holidays removed via region calendar). | Feed to workforce & AP accrual planning.                             |

---

## Tips & caveats

* Commodity price shocks ‚Äî Pass an extra column `commodity_index` (numeric) ‚Äî tree models will pick it up.

* Public holidays ‚Äî Send `"holiday":"NYD"` etc.; Prophet & trees exploit it.

* Variance bounds ‚Äî Add `"return_prediction_interval": true` to get 80 % / 95 % bands.

* Very new cost centre (< 30 pts) ‚Äî Service falls back to na√Øve mean and sets `"note":"cold-start"`.

---

## Next step
Automate this call on the last calendar day each month; push the business forecast into your rolling 13-week cash-flow model, and trigger re-forecast if actuals stray > 15 % outside the 80 % PI for two consecutive weeks.

---

# 4.3.4 /api/v1/ai/forecast_cost_improved

**Nine-month daily cost outlook**

### Purpose 
An extended variant of the generic_cost forecaster that also emits a Business Indicators block ‚Äì perfect for Finance & FP&A dashboards.

---

### Headers `X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yml
POST https://api.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/forecast_cost_improved
headers:
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret: <secret>
  Content-Type: application/json
```

### What problem it solves

| Business pain-point                      | How the endpoint helps                                            |
| ---------------------------------------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Need a longer horizon (up to 12 m)       | `forecast_period` now accepts 9+ months.                          |
| Want a one-line health read-out          | `business_indicators` summarises trend, volatility, CV, growth %. |
| Must reconcile calendar vs business days | Returns both roll-ups out-of-the-box.                             |

---

### Payload reference

| Path             | Type       | Req? | Purpose                  | Notes                            |
| ---------------- | ---------- | ---- | ------------------------ | -------------------------------- |
| forecast_period  | int ‚â• 1    | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Months to project        | e.g. 9                           |
| data[]           | array      | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Historic daily cost rows | ‚â• 60 rows for robust seasonality |
| ‚Ü≥ date           | YYYY-MM-DD | ‚úîÔ∏é   | ISO calendar date        | gaps auto-filled at 0            |
| ‚Ü≥ cost           | number     | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Cost amount              | currency agnostic                |

### How the engine chooses the ‚Äúbest algorithm‚Äù

1. Clean & enrich ‚Äì fill missing dates, create weekday/holiday dummies, lag & MA features.

2. Model bake-off ‚Äì ARIMA, STL-ETS, Prophet, TBATS, Gradient-Boost, Random-Forest, plus an Aggregation baseline that averages seasonal buckets (works surprisingly well on linear ramps).

3. Cross-validation ‚Äì rolling-window CV ‚Üí RMSE & MAE; lowest RMSE wins.

4. Indicators ‚Äì trend slope, œÉ, CV, growth %, cumulative cost for the full horizon.

---

### Key take-aways

| Signal                  | Read-out                            | Action                                           |
|------------------------ |------------------------------------ |--------------------------------------------------|
| Trend slope +4.78       | Costs rising ‚âà ‚Ç¨4.8 per day.        | Investigate drivers (commodity, wage).           |
| CV 0.13                 | Low volatility.                     | Suitable for straight-line accruals.             |
| Forecast growth +23.5 % | 9-month calendar total vs trailing. | Feed to cash-flow & variance tracker.            |

---

### Power-user tips

- **Scenario overlays** ‚Äì add `override_growth_pct` to shock the baseline (e.g. +10 % inflation).
- **Error bands** ‚Äì set `"return_prediction_interval": true` to get 80 % & 95 % PI.
- **Cost centres** ‚Äì batch 50+ series in one call via an array wrapper; each gets its own champion.
- **Alerting** ‚Äì compare actuals to the PI; if two consecutive business days breach the 80 % upper band, trigger spend-freeze workflow.

---

### Next step

Schedule this endpoint monthly via your orchestration tool (Airflow, Prefect‚Ä¶). Push the business series into your rolling 13-week cash forecast. Combine the growth % indicator with revenue projections to maintain a dynamic gross-margin outlook.

## 4.4.1 /api/v1/ai/inventory_history_improved
**Daily stock ledger + 360-degree inventory analytics**

**Purpose**‚ÄÉA single endpoint that converts raw purchases & sales into a rich inventory ledger, full KPI deck and aging dashboard.

### Headers `X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yml
POST https://api.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/inventory_history_improved
Headers:
```json
X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
X-Secret: <secret>
Content-Type: application/json
```

---

### What pain-point it fixes

| Operational headache                       | How the endpoint helps                                                                |
| ------------------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Need a day-by-day ledger for audit & BI    | `daily_inventory[]` rolls every purchase & sale into a running balance with %-changes |
| Finance wants turnover, DOS, volatility‚Ä¶   | `inventory_analysis{}` delivers 30+ KPIs with plain-English explanations              |
| Struggle to spot aging / obsolescence risk | `inventory_aging{}` splits lots into sold vs unsold with aging & risk buckets         |
| Need an all-in margin view                 | Price, cost & daily carrying cost feed margin %, EOQ, price sensitivity               |

---

### Payload reference

| Path                             | Type            | Req? | Purpose                   | Notes                       |
| -------------------------------- | --------------- | ---- | ------------------------- | --------------------------- |
| product_code                     | string / number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | SKU / article code        | returned verbatim           |
| sales_unity_cost                 | number          | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Unit COGS                 | currency-agnostic           |
| sales_unity_price                | number          | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Unit sell price           | used for margin, elasticity |
| inventory_daily_cost             | number          | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Holding cost / unit / day | for EOQ & efficiency flags  |
| lead_time_days                   | number          | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Replenishment lead time   | safety-stock calc           |
| inventory_initial_situation[]    | array           | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Opening stock snapshot    | exactly one row             |
| purchases[]                      | array           | ‚úîÔ∏é   | GRNs during the horizon   | any order                   |
| ‚Ü≥ purchase_date                  | YYYY-MM-DD      | ‚úîÔ∏é   |                           |                             |
| ‚Ü≥ purchase_quantity              | number          | ‚úîÔ∏é   | units                     |                             |
| sales[]                          | array           | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Shipments / invoices      | any order                   |
| ‚Ü≥ invoice_date                   | YYYY-MM-DD      | ‚úîÔ∏é   |                           |                             |
| ‚Ü≥ sales_quantity                 | number          | ‚úîÔ∏é   | units                     |                             |

---

### Minimal working example

```json
{
  "product_code": 38788,
  "sales_unity_cost": 25.50,
  "sales_unity_price": 60.73,
  "inventory_daily_cost": 0.15,
  "lead_time_days": 7.0,
  "inventory_initial_situation": [
    { "inventory_data": "2023-12-31", "inventory_quantity": 1050.0 }
  ],
  "purchases": [
    { "purchase_date": "2024-01-31", "purchase_quantity": 280.0 },
    { "purchase_date": "2024-02-28", "purchase_quantity": 240.0 },
    { "purchase_date": "2024-03-29", "purchase_quantity": 320.0 }
  ],
  "sales": [
    { "invoice_date": "2024-01-02", "sales_quantity":  5.0 },
    ‚ãØ
    { "invoice_date": "2024-03-15", "sales_quantity": 31.0 }
  ]
}
```

---

### How the engine works (under the hood)

* Calendar scaffold ‚Äì build a dense date index from min() to max(); back-fill zeros.

* Ledger build ‚Äì on each day: net_change = purchase ‚Äì sales, closing_inventory = prior + net_change.

* Activity tagging ‚Äì No Activity, Only Purchase, Only Sales, Purchase & Sales.

* Stats & classifications ‚Äì turnover, DOS, volatility, safety-stock, ABC, lifecycle, seasonality.

* Lot ageing ‚Äì FIFO consume purchases, track days until sold; flag unsold lots >90 days.

* Elasticity & price sensitivity ‚Äì simple OLS on price vs qty (if price series varied).

---

### Canonical response (excerpt)

```json
{
  "daily_inventory": [
    {
      "date": "2024-01-31",
      "purchase_quantity": 280,
      "sales_quantity": 0,
      "net_change": 280,
      "closing_inventory": 1216,
      "activity": "Only Purchase",
      "pct_change": 29.91
    },
    ‚ãØ
  ],
  "inventory_analysis": {
    "initial_inventory": { "value": 1050, "explanation": "‚Ä¶" },
    "cumulative_purchases": { "value": 840, "explanation": "‚Ä¶" },
    "cumulative_sales": { "value": 721, "explanation": "‚Ä¶" },
    "turnover_ratio_initial": { "value": 0.687, "turnover_description": "Very Low Turnover" },
    "inventory_days_of_supply": { "value": 123.97, "days_supply_description": "Very Sluggish Inventory" },
    ‚ãØ
  },
  "inventory_aging": {
    "sold_vs_unsold": {
      "sold_lots": {
        "summary": {
          "average_aging_days": 22,
          "std_aging_days": 12.73
        }
      },
      "unsold_lots": {
        "summary": { "weighted_average_current_age": 0 }
      }
    }
  },
  "product_details": {
    "product_code": 38788,
    "sales_unity_cost": 25.5,
    "sales_unity_price": 60.73,
    "inventory_daily_cost": 0.15
  },
  "processing_info": {
    "processing_time_seconds": 0.026,
    "calculation_date": "2025-05-21"
  }
}
```

---

### Reading the numbers ‚Äî quick insights for this sample

| Insight                | Metric                  | Why it matters                                      |
| ---------------------- | ----------------------- | --------------------------------------------------- |
| Excess-inventory alert | DOS = 124 days          | Capital locked; consider promo / PO deferral.       |
| Safety stock needed    | 42.7 units              | Cover 7-day lead time with demand œÉ ‚âà 9.8.          |
| Low turnover           | 0.69√ó initial stock     | SKU is slow-moving ‚Üí review range or price.         |
| Lot ageing healthy     | All sold within 31 days | No obsolescence yet; monitor the 320-unit lot.      |
| Price sensitivity      | CV margin ‚âà 0 ‚Üí Low     | Room for small price rises with minimal demand hit. |

---

### Core flow metrics
(See full list of KPIs in your source.)

---

### Next step

Feed `daily_inventory` into your BI layer for real-time stock dashboards.

Trigger alerts:
if `inventory_days_of_supply > 90` and `excess_inventory_risk = High` ‚Üí auto-suggest clearance promo.

Loop with forecasting: pair this ledger with `/api/forecast_units` to simulate future stock-outs & reorder points.

# 4.4.2 /api/v1/ai/inventory_optimization

**Find the sweet-spot between too much and too little stock**

### Purpose‚ÄÉ
A single endpoint that converts raw purchases & sales into a rich inventory ledger, full KPI deck and aging dashboard.

---

### Headers `X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yml
POST `https://api.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/inventory_optimization`
headers:
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret: <secret>
  Content-Type: application/json
```

---

### Why this endpoint exists

| Pain-point                                               | What the route delivers                                                                                    |
| -------------------------------------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| ‚ÄúHow many units should I order & when?‚Äù                  | `stock_optimization_and_replenishment{}` ‚Üí Re-order Point, Safety-Stock, EOQ & optimal order frequency.    |
| ‚ÄúAm I over-stocked‚Äêor‚Äêshort against the sales plan?‚Äù     | `inventory_analysis.excess_or_shortfall_analysis` compares today‚Äôs stock with the entire forecast horizon. |
| ‚ÄúNeed a single dashboard for demand trend, variability‚Ä¶‚Äù | `forecast_demand_analysis{}` ‚Äì growth %, volatility, above/below-average months, exhaustion month.         |
| Finance wants profit impact of shortfalls                | `financial_analysis.shortfall_cost_details` converts lost units ‚Üí lost margin.                             |
| Ops needs actionable alerts                              | `alerts{}` tell planners exactly what‚Äôs at risk.                                                           |

---

### Payload reference

| JSON path                                    | Type   | Req? | Purpose                   | Details                          |
| -------------------------------------------- | ------ | ---- | ------------------------- | -------------------------------- |
| inventory_last_position.closing_inventory    | number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Current on-hand qty       | baseline for coverage & turnover |
| inventory_last_position.last_count_date      | date   | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Date of stock count       | ISO YYYY-MM-DD                   |
| inventory_last_position.warehouse            | string | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Location label            | free text                        |
| product_details                              | object | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Static SKU metadata       | echoed back                      |
| forecast[]                                   |  array | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Monthly demand projection | yyyy-mm, value                   |
| lead_time_days                               | number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Replenishment lead time   | calendar days                    |
| daily_cost                                   | number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Holding cost / unit / day | local currency                   |
| ordering_cost                                | number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Cost per purchase order   | used in EOQ                      |
| sales_revenue                                | number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Unit sell price           | for revenue ratio                |
| sales_profit                                 | number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Unit contribution margin  | for shortfall loss               |
| buy_cost                                     | number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Unit purchase cost        | inventory value                  |

Tip: supply ‚â• 12 months of forecast for best EOQ & coverage logic.

---

### Minimal working example

```json
{
  "inventory_last_position": {
    "closing_inventory": 50000,
    "last_count_date": "2025-04-15",
    "warehouse": "Central-SP"
  },
  "product_details": {
    "product_code": "38788",
    "product_name": "Widget Pro XL",
    "category": "Industrial Components",
    "uom": "units",
    "supplier": "WidgetCo Brazil"
  },
  "forecast": [
    { "yyyy-mm": "2025-05", "value": 2500 },
    ‚ãØ
    { "yyyy-mm": "2027-04", "value": 3450 }
  ],
  "lead_time_days": 15,
  "daily_cost": 0.12,
  "ordering_cost": 150,
  "sales_revenue": 75,
  "sales_profit": 25,
  "buy_cost": 30
}
```

### Canonical response (key parts)

```json
{
  "inventory_analysis": {
    "inventory_coverage_ratio": {
      "months_of_inventory": 15.79,
      "days_of_inventory": 473.68,
      "description": "On-hand √∑ average monthly demand."
    },
    "excess_or_shortfall_analysis": {
      "stock_status": "Shortfall",
      "difference": 26000
    }
  },
  "stock_optimization_and_replenishment": {
    "reorder_point": 1678.68,
    "safety_stock": 95.35,
    "economic_order_quantity": 510.17,
    "optimal_order_frequency": 45.27,
    "inventory_turnover_ratio": 1.52
  },
  "forecast_demand_analysis": {
    "average_monthly_demand": 3166.67,
    "average_forecast_growth_rate": 1.83,
    "forecast_variability": {
      "coefficient_of_variation": 0.141
    },
    "cumulative_demand_projection": {
      "exhaustion_month": "2026-09"
    }
  },
  "financial_analysis": {
    "inventory_value": 1500000,
    "shortfall_cost_details": {
      "shortfall_quantity": 26000,
      "profit_loss": 650000
    }
  },
  "alerts": {
    "stock_status_alert": "Alert: Stock Shortfall ‚Äì immediate replenishment required."
  },
  "processing_info": {
    "processing_time_seconds": "0.005",
    "calculation_date": "2025-05-21"
  }
}
```

### Interpreting the sample

| What you learn          | Sample value       | Action                                                               |
| ----------------------- | ------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| Coverage                | 15.8 mo (474 days) | Looks ample, but cumulative demand shows shortfall later             |
| ROP                     | 1 679 u            | When projected balance drops to this level, place an order           |
| EOQ                     | 510 u              | Ideal order batch size to minimise total cost                        |
| Safety stock            | 95 u               | Covers 1.8 days at avg demand; low variability justifies lean buffer |
| Loss if not replenished | 650 k profit       | Quantifies urgency for finance & supply-chain                        |

---

### KPI (JSON path)

| KPI path                                                               | Technical meaning                      | Commercial meaning                                     |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------ |
| current_stock_level.closing_inventory                                  | Physical units on hand                 | Starting point for turnover & cash-tied-up discussions |
| inventory_coverage_ratio.months_of_inventory / days_of_inventory       | Stock √∑ avg monthly forecast (√ó30)     | How long you can keep selling before zero stock        |
| excess_or_shortfall_analysis.stock_status & difference                 | Compares stock to full forecast demand | Hidden lost-sales cost or excess carrying cost         |
| average_monthly_demand                                                 | Mean of forecast[].value              | Baseline for planning                                   |
| forecast_trends[].percentage_change                                    | MoM % delta                            | Demand acceleration signal                             |
| average_forecast_growth_rate                                           | Mean of MoM changes                    | Feed to revenue planning                               |
| seasonality_analysis.months_above_average                              | Month index > avg                      | Promo planning                                         |
| forecast_variability.coefficient_of_variation                          | std_dev √∑ mean                        | Safety stock guidance                                   |
| cumulative_demand_projection.exhaustion_month                          | First month demand > stock             | Deadline to order                                      |

---

### Replenishment Block

| KPI                        | Formula                                                          | Meaning                     |
| -------------------------- | ---------------------------------------------------------------- | --------------------------- |
| reorder_point              | (avg daily demand √ó lead-time) + safety_stock                    | PO trigger                  |
| safety_stock               | Z √ó œÉ(daily demand) √ó ‚àölead-time (Z‚âà1.65)                        | Noise buffer                |
| economic_order_quantity    | ‚àö((2 √ó annual demand √ó ordering_cost) / holding_cost per unit)   | Cost-efficient batch size   |
| optimal_order_frequency    | cumulative demand √∑ EOQ                                          | Orders needed               |
| inventory_turnover_ratio   | forecast_period_demand √∑ current_stock                           | Sales cash conversion speed |

---

### Classification Block

| KPI path                       | Meaning                                          |
| ------------------------------ | ------------------------------------------------ |
| demand_classification.value    | Rule-based demand tier                           |
| turnover_classification.value  | Rule-based on stock velocity                     |
| criticality.value              | Combines turnover & shortfall to prioritise SKUs |

---

### Risk & Sensitivity

| KPI path                                          | What it tells you                     |
| ------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------- |
| demand_sensitivity_analysis.demand_sensitivity    | CV grouped to High/Med/Low            |
| additional_indicators.stock_out_risk              | Heuristic flag for sales & SLA impact |

---

### Money Block

| KPI path                              | Meaning                       |
| ------------------------------------- | ----------------------------- |
| financial_analysis.inventory_value    | Capital locked                |
| profit_margin_percent                 | Contribution %                |
| sales_to_inventory_ratio              | ROI metric                    |
| shortfall_cost_details.profit_loss    | Lost margin from missed sales |

---

### Alerts

* Auto-generated flag: "Alert: Stock Shortfall ‚Äì immediate replenishment required."

---

### processing_info.processing_time_seconds

* Runtime: 0.005

---

### How to use the list

* Daily Ops: monitor ROP and auto-issue POs.

* Monthly S&OP: check forecast_variability, EOQ, seasonality.

* Quarterly Finance: review inventory_value, profit_loss, and sales_to_inventory_ratio.

---

#### Next step

* Create an automation that checks exhaustion_month weekly and warns 90 days in advance.

* Push ROP & EOQ into ERP/MRP for PO creation.

* Benchmark SKUs: average inventory_turnover_ratio and coefficient_of_variation to flag tuning candidates.

---

# 4.4.3 /api/v1/ai/nlp_openai_excess_inventory_report

**Turn raw inventory JSON into a board-ready excess-stock report**

### Purpose
One POST and you receive a fully drafted English-language report (tech insights + action plan) ready to paste into e-mail, slide deck or ERP note.

---

### Headers `X-Customer-Api-Id`, `X-Secret`

```yml
POST `https://api.abintel.ai/api/v1/ai/nlp_openai_excess_inventory_report`
headers:
  X-Customer-Api-Id: <uuid>
  X-Secret: <secret>
  Content-Type: application/json
```

---

### Why this endpoint exists

| Pain-point                                                             | What the route delivers |
| ---------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| Inventory analysts spend hours turning data into plain-English reports |`response.report_text` ‚áí 3-to-5-page narrative: product facts, stock/coverage, demand, financials, alerts, plus an excess-reduction playbook|
| Need to justify carrying costs to finance                              | `financial_analysis.excess_cost_details` is automatically interpreted and explained in prose.                                              |
| Execs want actionable strategies not just numbers                      | Section ‚ÄúStrategic Action Plan‚Äù (promo tiers, BOGO, flash-sale, etc.) with timeline, impact & KPIs.                                        |
| Avoid copy-paste errors between BI tools & docs                     |Endpoint takes exact same JSON your BI engine already produces(from `/inventory_optimization` or `/inventory_history`), no field mapping needed|

---

### Payload reference

| JSON path                              | Type          | Req? | Notes                                                                     |
| -------------------------------------- | ------------- | ---- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| `product_details.product_code`         | string/number | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Echoed back in report headline                                             |
| `product_details.product_name`         | string        | ‚úîÔ∏é   |                                                                            |
| `inventory_analysis`                   | object        | ‚úîÔ∏é   | At minimum include `current_stock_level`, `excess_or_shortfall_analysis`   |
| `forecast_demand_analysis`             | object        | ‚úîÔ∏é   | Needs `average_monthly_demand` and `forecast_trends` for trend commentary  |
| `stock_optimization_and_replenishment` | object        | ‚ú±    | Optional but recommended (ROP, EOQ, etc.)                                 |
| `financial_analysis`                   | object        | ‚ú±    | Required only if you want cost breakdown & profit impact paragraphs       |
| `management_insights` / `alerts`       | object        | ‚ú±    | Will be quoted verbatim inside the narrative if provided                  |

‚ú± = optional but the more you include, the richer the report.

---

Tip: All sections mirror the output of `/api/inventory_optimization`.
Pipe that JSON straight in here ‚Äì no transformation needed.

---
